Wait, I need to be more careful about the en passant square. The ep square is the square where the capturing pawn lands, which is one rank ahead of the captured pawn. So for white, the ep square is on rank 5 (0-indexed), and for black, it's on rank 2.

For white pawns capturing en passant:
- White pawn on rank 4, captures to ep square on rank 5
- The captured pawn is on the same file as the ep square, on rank 4

For black pawns capturing en passant:
- Black pawn on rank 3, captures to ep square on rank 2
- The captured pawn is on the same file as the ep square, on rank 3

So the en passant capture moves are:
- White: from (4, f), to (5, f±1) where (5, f±1) is the ep square
- Black: from (3, f), to (2, f±1) where (2, f±1) is the ep square

In my code, I check if `to == b.epSquare` for each potential capture square. This is correct.

But I should also check that the pawn is on the correct rank. Actually, the ep square is only set after a double pawn push, so it can only be on rank 2 or rank 5. A white pawn can only reach rank 4 by the time the ep square is on rank 5, and a black pawn can only reach rank 3 by the time the ep square is on rank 2. So the rank check is implicitly handled.

Wait, actually, that's not entirely true. A white pawn on rank 4 can capture en passant to an ep square on rank 5. But what if there's a white pawn on rank 3? It can't capture en passant because the target square (rank 5) is two ranks away. But my code only generates captures to sq+7 or sq+9 (one rank ahead), so this is fine.

One last thing: for the isAttacked function, I need to check if a square is attacked by any piece of a given color. Here's my approach:

```cpp
bool isAttacked(const Board& b, int sq, int byColor) {
    // Check pawn attacks
    if (byColor == WHITE) {
        // White pawns attack diagonally upward
        if (rankOf(sq) > 0) {
            if (fileOf(sq) > 0 && b.board[sq - 9] == makePiece(WHITE, PAWN)) return true;
            if (fileOf(sq) < 7 && b.board[sq - 7] == makePiece(WHITE, PAWN)) return true;
        }
    } else {
        // Black pawns attack diagonally downward
        if (rankOf(sq) < 7) {
            if (fileOf(sq) > 0 && b.board[sq + 7] == makePiece(BLACK, PAWN)) return true;
            if (fileOf(sq) < 7 && b.board[sq + 9] == makePiece(BLACK, PAWN)) return true;
        }
    }
    
    // Check knight attacks
    static const int knightOffsets[] = {-17, -15, -10, -6, 6, 10, 15, 17};
    for (int offset : knightOffsets) {
        int to = sq + offset;
        if (to >= 0 && to < 64 && abs(fileOf(to) - fileOf(sq)) <= 2) {
            if (b.board[to] == makePiece(byColor, KNIGHT)) return true;
        }
    }
    
    // Check king attacks
    static const int kingOffsets[] = {-9, -8, -7, -1, 1, 7, 8, 9};
    for (int offset : kingOffsets) {
        int to = sq + offset;
        if (to >= 0 && to < 64 && abs(fileOf(to) - fileOf(sq)) <= 1 && abs(rankOf(to) - rankOf(sq)) <= 1) {
            if (b.board[to] == makePiece(byColor, KING)) return true;
        }
    }
    
    // Check bishop/queen attacks (diagonals)
    static const int diagOffsets[] = {-9, -7, 7, 9};
    for (int offset : diagOffsets) {
        int to = sq + offset;
        int prevFile = fileOf(sq);
        while (to >= 0 && to < 64) {
            int toFile = fileOf(to);
            if (abs(toFile - prevFile) != 1) break; // file wrapped
            if (b.board[to] != EMPTY) {
                if (b.board[to] == makePiece(byColor, BISHOP) || b.board[to] == makePiece(byColor, QUEEN)) return true;
                break;
            }
            prevFile = toFile;
            to += offset;
        }
    }
    
    // Check rook/queen attacks (ranks and files)
    static const int straightOffsets[] = {-8, -1, 1, 8};
    for (int offset : straightOffsets) {
        int to = sq + offset;
        int prevFile = fileOf(sq);
        while (to >= 0 && to < 64) {
            int toFile = fileOf(to);
            if (offset == -1 || offset == 1) {
                if (abs(toFile - prevFile) != 1) break; // file wrapped
            }
            if (b.board[to] != EMPTY) {
                if (b.board[to] == makePiece(byColor, ROOK) || b.board[to] == makePiece(byColor, QUEEN)) return true;
                break;
            }
            prevFile = toFile;
            to += offset;
        }
    }
    
    return false;
}
```

Wait, the diagonal file wrapping check needs to be: when stepping diagonally, the file should change by exactly 1. If it changes by more (wrapping around the board edge), I should stop.

Let me reconsider. When stepping in direction +9 (right-up diagonal), from square (r, f), the next square is (r+1, f+1). The file changes by +1. If f was 7 (rightmost file), the next square wraps to (r+2, 0) or something like that. Let me check:

Hmm, the file wrapping check `abs(fileOf(to) - fileOf(to - dir)) != 1` is equivalent to checking if we've wrapped around. But this is a bit awkward. Let me use a simpler approach: check that the file of `to` differs from the file of `sq` by exactly the number of steps taken.

Actually, the simplest approach is to track the file as I go:

```cpp
// Check rook/queen attacks (left along rank)
{
    int to = sq - 1;
    int f = fileOf(sq) - 1;
    while (f >= 0) {
        if (b.board[to] != EMPTY) {
            if (b.board[to] == makePiece(byColor, ROOK) || b.board[to] == makePiece(byColor, QUEEN)) return true;
            break;

        f--;

    int f = fileOf(sq) + 1;

        if (b.board[to] != EMPTY) {
            if (b.board[to] == makePiece(byColor, ROOK) || b.board[to] == makePiece(byColor, QUEEN)) return true;
            break;
        }
        to++;
        f++;
    }
}
```

Actually, let me use a slightly different approach for move flags. Instead of using separate flag bits for castling and en passant, I'll use an enum:

```cpp
enum MoveFlags { FLAG_NORMAL = 0, FLAG_CASTLE = 1, FLAG_EP = 2 };
```

And promotion is stored separately in the promotion field (0 for no promotion, QUEEN/ROOK/BISHOP/KNIGHT for promotion).

A move can be:
- Normal move: flags = FLAG_NORMAL, promotion = 0
- Capture: flags = FLAG_NORMAL, promotion = 0, captured piece is on target square
- En passant: flags = FLAG_EP, promotion = 0
- Castling: flags = FLAG_CASTLE, promotion = 0
- Promotion: flags = FLAG_NORMAL, promotion = QUEEN/ROOK/BISHOP/KNIGHT
- Promotion capture: flags = FLAG_NORMAL, promotion = QUEEN/ROOK/BISHOP/KNIGHT, captured piece on target square

Wait, can en passant and promotion happen at the same time? No, because en passant captures on rank 3 or 6, and promotion happens on rank 1 or 8.

Can castling and promotion happen at the same time? No, because castling involves the king.

OK, the flags and promotion field cover all cases.

- Size: 1 << 24 = 16M entries
- Each entry: 16 bytes (key: uint64_t, score: int16_t, depth: int8_t, flag: uint8_t, move: uint16_t, padding)
- Total: 256MB

Actually, 256MB might be too much. Let me use 1 << 22 = 4M entries, which is 64MB. That should be sufficient.

```cpp
struct TTEntry {
    uint64_t key;
    int16_t score;
    int8_t depth;
    uint8_t flag;
    uint16_t bestFrom;
    uint16_t bestTo;
};

vector<TTEntry> tt(TT_SIZE);
```

I want to also make sure I handle the draw by 50-move rule. If the halfmove clock is >= 100 (50 full moves without a pawn move or capture), the game is drawn. I'll check this in the search.

Actually, in the FEN, halfmove is the half-move clock (number of half-moves since the last capture or pawn advance). If it reaches 100, it's a draw by the 50-move rule.

But in my search, I don't think I need to check this. The 50-move rule is typically claimed by a player, not automatically enforced. But for correctness, I'll add a check.

Actually, for a bot, it's important to avoid 50-move rule draws. If the bot is winning, it should try to make progress before the 50-move rule kicks in. If the bot is losing, it might want to delay. But for simplicity, I'll just return 0 if halfmove >= 100.

Let me start with the actual code now:

```cpp
#include <iostream>
#include <string>
#include <vector>
#include <array>
#include <chrono>
#include <cstring>
#include <algorithm>
#include <cstdint>
#include <random>
#include <atomic>

using namespace std;
using namespace std::chrono;

// ======================== CONSTANTS ========================

constexpr int EMPTY = 0;
constexpr int PAWN = 1, KNIGHT = 2, BISHOP = 3, ROOK = 4, QUEEN = 5, KING = 6;
constexpr int WHITE = 0, BLACK = 1;
constexpr int INF_SCORE = 50000;
constexpr int MATE_SCORE = 49000;
constexpr int MAX_DEPTH = 128;
constexpr int TT_SIZE = 1 << 24;

// Piece encoding: color * 6 + type (1-6 for white, 7-12 for black)
inline int makePiece(int color, int type) { return color * 6 + type; }
inline int pieceType(int piece) { return piece == 0 ? 0 : ((piece - 1) % 6) + 1; }
inline int pieceColor(int piece) { return piece == 0 ? 0 : (piece - 1) / 6; }

// Square encoding: rank * 8 + file (0-63)
inline int rankOf(int sq) { return sq >> 3; }
inline int fileOf(int sq) { return sq & 7; }
inline int mirrorSq(int sq) { return sq ^ 56; }

string sqToStr(int sq) {
    return string(1, 'a' + fileOf(sq)) + string(1, '1' + rankOf(sq));
}

// Material values
constexpr int PIECE_VAL[7] = {0, 100, 320, 330, 500, 900, 20000};

// Piece-square tables (from white's perspective, a1=index 0)
// ... (I'll include the tables)

// ======================== ZOBRIST ========================

uint64_t ZOBRIST_PIECE[13][64];
uint64_t ZOBRIST_CASTLE[16];
uint64_t ZOBRIST_EP[8];
uint64_t ZOBRIST_SIDE;

void initZobrist() {
    mt19937_64 rng(0x12345678);
    for (int p = 0; p < 13; p++)
        for (int sq = 0; sq < 64; sq++)
            ZOBRIST_PIECE[p][sq] = rng();
    for (int i = 0; i < 16; i++)
        ZOBRIST_CASTLE[i] = rng();
    for (int i = 0; i < 8; i++)
        ZOBRIST_EP[i] = rng();
    ZOBRIST_SIDE = rng();
}

// ======================== MOVE ========================

enum MoveFlags { FLAG_NORMAL = 0, FLAG_CASTLE = 1, FLAG_EP = 2 };

struct Move {
    int from, to;
    int promotion; // 0 or QUEEN/ROOK/BISHOP/KNIGHT
    int flags;     // FLAG_NORMAL, FLAG_CASTLE, FLAG_EP
    int score;     // for move ordering
    
    bool operator==(const Move& o) const {
        return from == o.from && to == o.to && promotion == o.promotion && flags == o.flags;
    }
};

// ======================== BOARD ========================

struct Board {
    int board[64];
    int side;
    int castling;  // bit0=WK, bit1=WQ, bit2=BK, bit3=BQ
    int epSquare;  // -1 if none
    int halfmove;
    int fullmove;
    int kingSq[2];
    uint64_t hash;
    
    void computeHash() {
        hash = 0;
        for (int sq = 0; sq < 64; sq++)
            if (board[sq] != EMPTY)
                hash ^= ZOBRIST_PIECE[board[sq]][sq];
        if (side == BLACK) hash ^= ZOBRIST_SIDE;
        hash ^= ZOBRIST_CASTLE[castling];
        if (epSquare >= 0) hash ^= ZOBRIST_EP[fileOf(epSquare)];
    }
};

// ======================== UNDO INFO ========================

struct UndoInfo {
    int captured;
    int capturedSq;
    int castling;
    int epSquare;
    int halfmove;
    uint64_t hash;
};

// ======================== FEN PARSING ========================

Board parseFEN(const string& fen) {
    Board b;
    memset(b.board, 0, sizeof(b.board));
    b.castling = 0;
    b.epSquare = -1;
    b.halfmove = 0;
    b.fullmove = 1;
    
    int i = 0;
    // Piece placement
    int sq = 56; // start from a8
    while (i < fen.size() && fen[i] != ' ') {
        if (fen[i] == '/') {
            sq -= 16; // go to next rank down
        } else if (fen[i] >= '1' && fen[i] <= '8') {
            sq += fen[i] - '0';
        } else {
            int piece = 0;
            switch (fen[i]) {
                case 'P': piece = makePiece(WHITE, PAWN); break;
                case 'N': piece = makePiece(WHITE, KNIGHT); break;
                case 'B': piece = makePiece(WHITE, BISHOP); break;
                case 'R': piece = makePiece(WHITE, ROOK); break;
                case 'Q': piece = makePiece(WHITE, QUEEN); break;
                case 'K': piece = makePiece(WHITE, KING); break;
                case 'p': piece = makePiece(BLACK, PAWN); break;
                case 'n': piece = makePiece(BLACK, KNIGHT); break;
                case 'b': piece = makePiece(BLACK, BISHOP); break;
                case 'r': piece = makePiece(BLACK, ROOK); break;
                case 'q': piece = makePiece(BLACK, QUEEN); break;
                case 'k': piece = makePiece(BLACK, KING); break;
            }
            b.board[sq] = piece;
            if (pieceType(piece) == KING) {
                b.kingSq[pieceColor(piece)] = sq;
            }
            sq++;
        }
        i++;
    }
    
    // Side to move
    i++; // skip space
    b.side = (fen[i] == 'w') ? WHITE : BLACK;
    i += 2; // skip side and space
    
    // Castling
    if (fen[i] == '-') {
        i++;
    } else {
        while (i < fen.size() && fen[i] != ' ') {
            switch (fen[i]) {
                case 'K': b.castling |= 1; break;
                case 'Q': b.castling |= 2; break;
                case 'k': b.castling |= 4; break;
                case 'q': b.castling |= 8; break;
            }
            i++;
        }
    }
    i++; // skip space
    
    // En passant
    if (fen[i] == '-') {
        b.epSquare = -1;
        i++;
    } else {
        int file = fen[i] - 'a';
        int rank = fen[i + 1] - '1';
        b.epSquare = rank * 8 + file;
        i += 2;
    }
    
    // Halfmove clock and fullmove number (optional)
    if (i < fen.size() && fen[i] == ' ') {
        i++;
        int hm = 0;
        while (i < fen.size() && fen[i] >= '0' && fen[i] <= '9') {
            hm = hm * 10 + fen[i] - '0';
            i++;
        }
        b.halfmove = hm;
        if (i < fen.size() && fen[i] == ' ') {
            i++;
            int fm = 0;
            while (i < fen.size() && fen[i] >= '0' && fen[i] <= '9') {
                fm = fm * 10 + fen[i] - '0';
                i++;
            }
            b.fullmove = fm;
        }
    }
    
    b.computeHash();
    return b;
}

// ======================== ATTACK DETECTION ========================

bool isAttacked(const Board& b, int sq, int byColor) {
    // Pawn attacks
    if (byColor == WHITE) {
        if (rankOf(sq) > 0) {
            if (fileOf(sq) > 0 && b.board[sq - 9] == makePiece(WHITE, PAWN)) return true;
            if (fileOf(sq) < 7 && b.board[sq - 7] == makePiece(WHITE, PAWN)) return true;
        }
    } else {
        if (rankOf(sq) < 7) {
            if (fileOf(sq) > 0 && b.board[sq + 7] == makePiece(BLACK, PAWN)) return true;
            if (fileOf(sq) < 7 && b.board[sq + 9] == makePiece(BLACK, PAWN)) return true;
        }
    }
    
    // Knight attacks
    static const int knightOffsets[] = {-17, -15, -10, -6, 6, 10, 15, 17};
    int knight = makePiece(byColor, KNIGHT);
    for (int offset : knightOffsets) {
        int to = sq + offset;
        if (to >= 0 && to < 64 && abs(fileOf(to) - fileOf(sq)) <= 2 && abs(rankOf(to) - rankOf(sq)) <= 2) {
            if (b.board[to] == knight) return true;
        }
    }
    
    // King attacks
    static const int kingOffsets[] = {-9, -8, -7, -1, 1, 7, 8, 9};
    int king = makePiece(byColor, KING);
    for (int offset : kingOffsets) {
        int to = sq + offset;
        if (to >= 0 && to < 64 && abs(fileOf(to) - fileOf(sq)) <= 1 && abs(rankOf(to) - rankOf(sq)) <= 1) {
            if (b.board[to] == king) return true;
        }
    }
    
    // Bishop/Queen attacks (diagonals)
    int bishop = makePiece(byColor, BISHOP);
    int queen = makePiece(byColor, QUEEN);
    static const int diagDirs[] = {-9, -7, 7, 9};
    for (int dir : diagDirs) {
        int to = sq + dir;
        int prevFile = fileOf(sq);
        while (to >= 0 && to < 64) {
            int toFile = fileOf(to);
            if (abs(toFile - prevFile) != 1) break;
            if (b.board[to] != EMPTY) {
                if (b.board[to] == bishop || b.board[to] == queen) return true;
                break;
            }
            prevFile = toFile;
            to += dir;
        }
    }
    
    // Rook/Queen attacks (ranks and files)
    int rook = makePiece(byColor, ROOK);
    // Ranks (left and right)
    {
        int to = sq - 1;
        while (to >= 0 && fileOf(to) < fileOf(to + 1)) { // didn't wrap
            if (b.board[to] != EMPTY) {
                if (b.board[to] == rook || b.board[to] == queen) return true;
                break;
            }
            to--;
        }
    }
    {
        int to = sq + 1;
        while (to < 64 && fileOf(to) > fileOf(to - 1)) { // didn't wrap
            if (b.board[to] != EMPTY) {
                if (b.board[to] == rook || b.board[to] == queen) return true;
                break;
            }
            to++;
        }
    }
    // Files (up and down)
    {
        int to = sq + 8;
        while (to < 64) {
            if (b.board[to] != EMPTY) {
                if (b.board[to] == rook || b.board[to] == queen) return true;
                break;
            }
            to += 8;
        }
    }
    {
        int to = sq - 8;
        while (to >= 0) {
            if (b.board[to] != EMPTY) {
                if (b.board[to] == rook || b.board[to] == queen) return true;
                break;
            }
            to -= 8;
        }
    }
    
    return false;
}

// ======================== MOVE GENERATION ========================

void addMove(vector<Move>& moves, int from, int to, int promotion, int flags) {
    moves.push_back({from, to, promotion, flags, 0});
}

vector<Move> generatePseudoLegal(const Board& b) {
    vector<Move> moves;
    moves.reserve(256);
    
    for (int sq = 0; sq < 64; sq++) {
        int piece = b.board[sq];
        if (piece == EMPTY || pieceColor(piece) != b.side) continue;
        int pt = pieceType(piece);
        
        switch (pt) {
            case PAWN: {
                if (b.side == WHITE) {
                    // Single push
                    int to = sq + 8;
                    if (to < 64 && b.board[to] == EMPTY) {
                        if (rankOf(to) == 7) {
                            for (int p : {QUEEN, ROOK, BISHOP, KNIGHT})
                                addMove(moves, sq, to, p, FLAG_NORMAL);
                        } else {
                            addMove(moves, sq, to, 0, FLAG_NORMAL);
                        }
                        // Double push
                        if (rankOf(sq) == 1) {
                            int to2 = sq + 16;
                            if (b.board[to2] == EMPTY) {
                                addMove(moves, sq, to2, 0, FLAG_NORMAL);
                            }
                        }
                    }
                    // Captures
                    if (fileOf(sq) > 0) {
                        to = sq + 7;
                        if (to < 64) {
                            if (b.board[to] != EMPTY && pieceColor(b.board[to]) == BLACK) {
                                if (rankOf(to) == 7) {
                                    for (int p : {QUEEN, ROOK, BISHOP, KNIGHT})
                                        addMove(moves, sq, to, p, FLAG_NORMAL);
                                } else {
                                    addMove(moves, sq, to, 0, FLAG_NORMAL);
                                }
                            }
                            if (to == b.epSquare) {
                                addMove(moves, sq, to, 0, FLAG_EP);
                            }
                        }
                    }
                    if (fileOf(sq) < 7) {
                        to = sq + 9;
                        if (to < 64) {
                            if (b.board[to] != EMPTY && pieceColor(b.board[to]) == BLACK) {
                                if (rankOf(to) == 7) {
                                    for (int p : {QUEEN, ROOK, BISHOP, KNIGHT})
                                        addMove(moves, sq, to, p, FLAG_NORMAL);
                                } else {
                                    addMove(moves, sq, to, 0, FLAG_NORMAL);
                                }
                            }
                            if (to == b.epSquare) {
                                addMove(moves, sq, to, 0, FLAG_EP);
                            }
                        }
                    }
                } else { // BLACK
                    int to = sq - 8;
                    if (to >= 0 && b.board[to] == EMPTY) {
                        if (rankOf(to) == 0) {
                            for (int p : {QUEEN, ROOK, BISHOP, KNIGHT})
                                addMove(moves, sq, to, p, FLAG_NORMAL);
                        } else {
                            addMove(moves, sq, to, 0, FLAG_NORMAL);
                        }
                        if (rankOf(sq) == 6) {
                            int to2 = sq - 16;
                            if (b.board[to2] == EMPTY) {
                                addMove(moves, sq, to2, 0, FLAG_NORMAL);
                            }
                        }
                    }
                    if (fileOf(sq) > 0) {
                        to = sq - 9;
                        if (to >= 0) {
                            if (b.board[to] != EMPTY && pieceColor(b.board[to]) == WHITE) {
                                if (rankOf(to) == 0) {
                                    for (int p : {QUEEN, ROOK, BISHOP, KNIGHT})
                                        addMove(moves, sq, to, p, FLAG_NORMAL);
                                } else {
                                    addMove(moves, sq, to, 0, FLAG_NORMAL);
                                }
                            }
                            if (to == b.epSquare) {
                                addMove(moves, sq, to, 0, FLAG_EP);
                            }
                        }
                    }
                    if (fileOf(sq) < 7) {
                        to = sq - 7;
                        if (to >= 0) {
                            if (b.board[to] != EMPTY && pieceColor(b.board[to]) == WHITE) {
                                if (rankOf(to) == 0) {
                                    for (int p : {QUEEN, ROOK, BISHOP, KNIGHT})
                                        addMove(moves, sq, to, p, FLAG_NORMAL);
                                } else {
                                    addMove(moves, sq, to, 0, FLAG_NORMAL);
                                }
                            }
                            if (to == b.epSquare) {
                                addMove(moves, sq, to, 0, FLAG_EP);
                            }
                        }
                    }
                }
                break;
            }
            case KNIGHT: {
                static const int offsets[] = {-17, -15, -10, -6, 6, 10, 15, 17};
                for (int offset : offsets) {
                    int to = sq + offset;
                    if (to >= 0 && to < 64 && abs(fileOf(to) - fileOf(sq)) <= 2) {
                        if (b.board[to] == EMPTY || pieceColor(b.board[to]) != b.side) {
                            addMove(moves, sq, to, 0, FLAG_NORMAL);
                        }
                    }
                }
                break;
            }
            case BISHOP: {
                static const int dirs[] = {-9, -7, 7, 9};
                for (int dir : dirs) {
                    int to = sq + dir;
                    int prevFile = fileOf(sq);
                    while (to >= 0 && to < 64) {
                        int toFile = fileOf(to);
                        if (abs(toFile - prevFile) != 1) break;
                        if (b.board[to] != EMPTY) {
                            if (pieceColor(b.board[to]) != b.side)
                                addMove(moves, sq, to, 0, FLAG_NORMAL);
                            break;
                        }
                        addMove(moves, sq, to, 0, FLAG_NORMAL);
                        prevFile = toFile;
                        to += dir;
                    }
                }
                break;
            }
            case ROOK: {
                // Left
                {
                    int to = sq - 1;
                    while (to >= 0 && fileOf(to) < fileOf(to + 1)) {
                        if (b.board[to] != EMPTY) {
                            if (pieceColor(b.board[to]) != b.side)
                                addMove(moves, sq, to, 0, FLAG_NORMAL);
                            break;
                        }
                        addMove(moves, sq, to, 0, FLAG_NORMAL);
                        to--;
                    }
                }
                // Right
                {
                    int to = sq + 1;
                    while (to < 64 && fileOf(to) > fileOf(to - 1)) {
                        if (b.board[to] != EMPTY) {
                            if (pieceColor(b.board[to]) != b.side)
                                addMove(moves, sq, to, 0, FLAG_NORMAL);
                            break;
                        }
                        addMove(moves, sq, to, 0, FLAG_NORMAL);
                        to++;
                    }
                }
                // Up
                {
                    int to = sq + 8;
                    while (to < 64) {
                        if (b.board[to] != EMPTY) {
                            if (pieceColor(b.board[to]) != b.side)
                                addMove(moves, sq, to, 0, FLAG_NORMAL);
                            break;
                        }
                        addMove(moves, sq, to, 0, FLAG_NORMAL);
                        to += 8;
                    }
                }
                // Down
                {
                    int to = sq - 8;
                    while (to >= 0) {
                        if (b.board[to] != EMPTY) {
                            if (pieceColor(b.board[to]) != b.side)
                                addMove(moves, sq, to, 0, FLAG_NORMAL);
                            break;
                        }
                        addMove(moves, sq, to, 0, FLAG_NORMAL);
                        to -= 8;
                    }
                }
                break;
            }
            case QUEEN: {
                // Diagonals (like bishop)
                {
                    static const int dirs[] = {-9, -7, 7, 9};
                    for (int dir : dirs) {
                        int to = sq + dir;
                        int prevFile = fileOf(sq);
                        while (to >= 0 && to < 64) {
                            int toFile = fileOf(to);
                            if (abs(toFile - prevFile) != 1) break;
                            if (b.board[to] != EMPTY) {
                                if (pieceColor(b.board[to]) != b.side)
                                    addMove(moves, sq, to, 0, FLAG_NORMAL);
                                break;
                            }
                            addMove(moves, sq, to, 0, FLAG_NORMAL);
                            prevFile = toFile;
                            to += dir;
                        }
                    }
                }
                // Straight lines (like rook)
                {
                    int to = sq - 1;
                    while (to >= 0 && fileOf(to) < fileOf(to + 1)) {
                        if (b.board[to] != EMPTY) {
                            if (pieceColor(b.board[to]) != b.side)
                                addMove(moves, sq, to, 0, FLAG_NORMAL);
                            break;
                        }
                        addMove(moves, sq, to, 0, FLAG_NORMAL);
                        to--;
                    }
                }
                // ... (similar for other directions)
                break;
            }
            case KING: {
                static const int offsets[] = {-9, -8, -7, -1, 1, 7, 8, 9};
                for (int offset : offsets) {
                    int to = sq + offset;
                    if (to >= 0 && to < 64 && abs(fileOf(to) - fileOf(sq)) <= 1 && abs(rankOf(to) - rankOf(sq)) <= 1) {
                        if (b.board[to] == EMPTY || pieceColor(b.board[to]) != b.side) {
                            addMove(moves, sq, to, 0, FLAG_NORMAL);
                        }
                    }
                }
                // Castling
                if (b.side == WHITE) {
                    if ((b.castling & 1) && b.board[5] == EMPTY && b.board[6] == EMPTY) {
                        if (!isAttacked(b, 4, BLACK) && !isAttacked(b, 5, BLACK) && !isAttacked(b, 6, BLACK)) {
                            addMove(moves, 4, 6, 0, FLAG_CASTLE);
                        }
                    }
                    if ((b.castling & 2) && b.board[3] == EMPTY && b.board[2] == EMPTY && b.board[1] == EMPTY) {
                        if (!isAttacked(b, 4, BLACK) && !isAttacked(b, 3, BLACK) && !isAttacked(b, 2, BLACK)) {
                            addMove(moves, 4, 2, 0, FLAG_CASTLE);
                        }
                    }
                } else {
                    if ((b.castling & 4) && b.board[61] == EMPTY && b.board[62] == EMPTY) {
                        if (!isAttacked(b, 60, WHITE) && !isAttacked(b, 61, WHITE) && !isAttacked(b, 62, WHITE)) {
                            addMove(moves, 60, 62, 0, FLAG_CASTLE);
                        }
                    }
                    if ((b.castling & 8) && b.board[59] == EMPTY && b.board[58] == EMPTY && b.board[57] == EMPTY) {
                        if (!isAttacked(b, 60, WHITE) && !isAttacked(b, 59, WHITE) && !isAttacked(b, 58, WHITE)) {
                            addMove(moves, 60, 58, 0, FLAG_CASTLE);
                        }
                    }
                }
                break;
            }
        }
    }
    
    return moves;
}
```

```cpp

```

Wait, I also need to think about how to detect check and checkmate for the output move notation. After finding the best move, I need to:
1. Make the best move on a copy of the board
2. Check if the opponent's king is in check
3. If in check, generate all legal moves for the opponent
4. If no legal moves, it's checkmate (#); otherwise, it's check (+)

This requires a legal move generation function, which I need to implement.

```cpp
vector<Move> generateLegalMoves(Board& b) {
    vector<Move> legal;
    vector<Move> pseudo = generatePseudoLegal(b);
    for (auto& m : pseudo) {
        UndoInfo undo = makeMove(b, m);
        // After makeMove, b.side has flipped. Check if the previous mover's king is in check.
        if (!isAttacked(b, b.kingSq[b.side ^ 1], b.side)) {
            legal.push_back(m);
        }
        unmakeMove(b, m, undo);
    }
    return legal;
}
```

Wait, after makeMove, b.side has flipped. The side that just moved is b.side ^ 1. I need to check if b.side ^ 1's king is attacked by b.side's pieces. But wait, after makeMove, it's now b.side's turn. So I'm checking if the side that just moved (b.side ^ 1) left their king in check.

Hmm, let me re-read my isAttacked function. `isAttacked(b, sq, byColor)` checks if sq is attacked by any piece of color `byColor`.

After makeMove, b.side is the side whose turn it is now (the opponent of the side that just moved). The side that just moved is b.side ^ 1. Their king is at b.kingSq[b.side ^ 1].

I need to check if the side that just moved left their own king in check. That means checking if b.kingSq[b.side ^ 1] is attacked by b.side (the current side to move).

So: `isAttacked(b, b.kingSq[b.side ^ 1], b.side)`.

If this is true, the move was illegal.

Wait, that doesn't sound right. If white just moved, and it's now black's turn, I need to check if white's king is in check. White's king is at b.kingSq[WHITE] = b.kingSq[b.side ^ 1] (since b.side is now BLACK). And I need to check if black's pieces attack white's king. That's isAttacked(b, b.kingSq[WHITE], BLACK) = isAttacked(b, b.kingSq[b.side ^ 1], b.side).

Yes, that's correct. If white's king is attacked by black after white's move, the move is illegal.

OK, the legal move generation is correct.

Now, for the check/checkmate detection:
After making the best move, I need to check if the opponent is in check:
- Opponent is b.side (after makeMove)
- Opponent's king is at b.kingSq[b.side]
- I need to check if b.kingSq[b.side] is attacked by b.side ^ 1 (the side that just moved)
- So: `isAttacked(b, b.kingSq[b.side], b.side ^ 1)`

If the opponent is in check, I then check if it's checkmate by generating all legal moves for the opponent. If there are no legal moves, it's checkmate.

One thing: in the makeMove function, when I handle en passant, I need to make sure that the en passant square is valid. The en passant square is set by the FEN parser or by a double pawn push in a previous move. It should only be valid for one move (the move immediately after the double pawn push). I clear it at the beginning of makeMove and only set it if the current move is a double pawn push.

Wait, I already handle this:
```cpp
b.epSquare = -1; // clear en passant
if (pt == PAWN && abs(rankOf(m.to) - rankOf(m.from)) == 2) {
    b.epSquare = (m.from + m.to) / 2;
}
```

This is correct. The en passant square is only set for one move.

But wait, there's a subtlety: the en passant square should only be set if there's an enemy pawn adjacent to the double-pushed pawn. According to the FIDE rules, en passant is only possible if there's a pawn that can capture. However, in chess programming, it's common to set the en passant square regardless, because the Zobrist hash distinguishes positions with and without en passant. If I only set the en passant square when there's an adjacent enemy pawn, I might miss some hash collisions.

For correctness and simplicity, I'll set the en passant square after every double pawn push, regardless of whether there's an adjacent enemy pawn. This is the standard approach in chess engines.

- 15: (r+2, f-1) if f >= 1 and r <= 5
- 17: (r+2, f+1) if f <= 6 and r <= 5

I'm using the check `abs(fileOf(to) - fileOf(sq)) <= 2` to validate the file distance. But this allows file distances of 0 and 2 (not 1), which is correct for some offsets but not all. Let me verify:

For offset -17: from (r, f) to (r-2, f-1). File distance = 1. My check allows 0, 1, 2. So 1 is allowed. Correct.
For offset -10: from (r, f) to (r-1, f-2). File distance = 2. My check allows 0, 1, 2. So 2 is allowed. Correct.
For offset +9 (not a knight offset, but let me check): from (r, f) to (r+1, f+1). File distance = 1. This is not a knight offset, but my check would allow it. However, +9 is not in the knight offset list, so it wouldn't be checked.

Wait, but what about wrapping? If f = 0 and offset = -17, then to = sq - 17. fileOf(to) could be 7 (wrapped from file 0 to file 7 across the rank boundary). abs(7 - 0) = 7 > 2, so my check would correctly reject it.

If f = 1 and offset = -17, then to = sq - 17 = (r-2)*8 + f-1 = (r-2)*8 + 0. fileOf(to) = 0. abs(0 - 1) = 1 <= 2. Correct, this is a valid knight move.

If f = 7 and offset = 17, then to = sq + 17 = (r+2)*8 + f+1 = (r+2)*8 + 8 = (r+3)*8 + 0. fileOf(to) = 0. abs(0 - 7) = 7 > 2. Rejected. But wait, the knight should be able to go from (r, 7) to (r+2, 8)? No, file 8 doesn't exist. So the move is invalid. And to = (r+3)*8 + 0, which is on a different rank than expected (r+3 instead of r+2) and a different file (0 instead of 8). So my check correctly rejects it.

What if f = 6 and offset = 17? to = sq + 17 = (r+2)*8 + 7. fileOf(to) = 7. abs(7 - 6) = 1 <= 2. This is a valid knight move (r, 6) to (r+2, 7). Correct!

OK, the knight move generation with the `abs(fileOf(to) - fileOf(sq)) <= 2` check is correct.

```cpp

```

This ensures that both file and rank distances are at most 2, which is correct for knight moves.

But actually, the rank check is redundant because:
- If `to >= 0 && to < 64`, the rank is between 0 and 7
- The knight moves at most 2 ranks
- The original rank is between 0 and 7
- So the rank distance is at most 7

But wrapping could make the rank distance larger than expected. For example, from rank 1, offset -17 gives rank -1, which wraps to... well, the square would be negative, so `to >= 0` would catch it.

From rank 6, offset +17 gives rank 8, which would be out of bounds (to >= 64 catches it).

From rank 6, offset +10: to = (6*8+f) + 10 = 58+f. If f <= 5, to = 58 to 63. This is valid. rankOf(to) = (58+f) / 8. For f=0: 58/8 = 7. rankOf(to) = 7, rankOf(sq) = 6. abs(7-6) = 1. Correct (knight moves 1 rank).

Wait, I also want to make sure my evaluation is correct. Let me think about it one more time.

```cpp
int evaluate(const Board& b) {
    int score = 0;
    int bishopCount[2] = {0, 0};
    
    for (int sq = 0; sq < 64; sq++) {
        int piece = b.board[sq];
        if (piece == EMPTY) continue;
        int pt = pieceType(piece);
        int pc = pieceColor(piece);
        int val = PIECE_VAL[pt];
        int pst = PST[pt][pc == WHITE ? sq : mirrorSq(sq)];
        if (pc == WHITE) score += val + pst;
        else score -= val + pst;
        if (pt == BISHOP) bishopCount[pc]++;
    }
    
    // Bishop pair bonus
    if (bishopCount[WHITE] >= 2) score += 30;
    if (bishopCount[BLACK] >= 2) score -= 30;
    
    // Return from side to move's perspective
    return b.side == WHITE ? score : -score;
}
```

This is correct. The score is computed from white's perspective, then negated if it's black's turn (for negamax).

For the search, I'll use the following structure:

```cpp
// Global search state
Board gBoard;
atomic<bool> gSearchStopped(false);
steady_clock::time_point gStartTime;
int gTimeLimit; // milliseconds
int gNodeCount;
Move gBestMove;
int gBestScore;

// Killer moves: 2 per ply
Move gKillers[MAX_DEPTH][2];

// History heuristic
int gHistory[64][64];

// Transposition table
struct TTEntry {
    uint64_t key;
    int16_t score;
    int8_t depth;
    uint8_t flag; // 0=exact, 1=lower, 2=upper
    uint8_t bestFrom, bestTo;
};
vector<TTEntry> gTT;

// TT flags
constexpr int TT_EXACT = 0, TT_LOWER = 1, TT_UPPER = 2;
```

For the iterative deepening:

```cpp
void iterativeDeepening() {
    gBestMove = {0, 0, 0, 0, 0}; // no move yet
    gBestScore = -INF_SCORE;
    
    for (int depth = 1; depth <= MAX_DEPTH; depth++) {
        int score = alphaBeta(gBoard, depth, -INF_SCORE, INF_SCORE, 0);
        
        if (gSearchStopped) break;
        
        gBestScore = score;
        
        // Check time
        auto elapsed = duration_cast<milliseconds>(steady_clock::now() - gStartTime).count();
        if (elapsed > gTimeLimit / 2) break; // don't start a new iteration if we've used more than half the time
    }
}
```

For the alpha-beta search:

```cpp
int alphaBeta(Board& b, int depth, int alpha, int beta, int ply) {
    if (gSearchStopped) return 0;
    if ((++gNodeCount & 4095) == 0) {
        auto elapsed = duration_cast<milliseconds>(steady_clock::now() - gStartTime).count();
        if (elapsed >= gTimeLimit) {
            gSearchStopped = true;
            return 0;
        }
    }
    
    // Draw by 50-move rule
    if (b.halfmove >= 100) return 0;
    
    // Check extension
    bool inCheck = isAttacked(b, b.kingSq[b.side], b.side ^ 1);
    if (inCheck) depth++;
    
    // Quiescence search at depth 0
    if (depth <= 0) return quiescence(b, alpha, beta, ply);
    
    // Transposition table probe
    uint64_t key = b.hash;
    TTEntry* ttEntry = nullptr;
    int ttIndex = key & (gTT.size() - 1);
    if (gTT[ttIndex].key == key) {
        ttEntry = &gTT[ttIndex];
        if (ttEntry->depth >= depth) {
            int ttScore = ttEntry->score;
            // Adjust mate scores
            if (ttScore > MATE_SCORE - 100) ttScore -= ply;
            if (ttScore < -MATE_SCORE + 100) ttScore += ply;
            
            if (ttEntry->flag == TT_EXACT) return ttScore;
            if (ttEntry->flag == TT_LOWER && ttScore >= beta) return ttScore;
            if (ttEntry->flag == TT_UPPER && ttScore <= alpha) return ttScore;
        }
    }
    
    // Null move pruning
    if (depth >= 3 && !inCheck && ply > 0) {
        // Make null move
        int oldEp = b.epSquare;
        b.side ^= 1;
        b.epSquare = -1;
        b.hash ^= ZOBRIST_SIDE;
        if (oldEp >= 0) b.hash ^= ZOBRIST_EP[fileOf(oldEp)];
        
        int score = -alphaBeta(b, depth - 3, -beta, -beta + 1, ply + 1);
        
        // Unmake null move
        b.side ^= 1;
        b.epSquare = oldEp;
        b.hash ^= ZOBRIST_SIDE;
        if (oldEp >= 0) b.hash ^= ZOBRIST_EP[fileOf(oldEp)];
        
        if (gSearchStopped) return 0;
        if (score >= beta) return beta;
    }
    
    // Generate moves
    vector<Move> moves = generatePseudoLegal(b);
    
    // Move ordering
    for (auto& m : moves) {
        m.score = 0;
        // TT move
        if (ttEntry && m.from == ttEntry->bestFrom && m.to == ttEntry->bestTo) {
            m.score = 1000000;
            continue;
        }
        // Captures: MVV-LVA
        int captured = b.board[m.to];
        if (m.flags == FLAG_EP) captured = makePiece(b.side ^ 1, PAWN);
        if (captured != EMPTY) {
            m.score = 100000 + PIECE_VAL[pieceType(captured)] * 10 - PIECE_VAL[pieceType(b.board[m.from])];
            continue;
        }
        // Killer moves
        if (m.from == gKillers[ply][0].from && m.to == gKillers[ply][0].to) {
            m.score = 90000;
            continue;
        }
        if (m.from == gKillers[ply][1].from && m.to == gKillers[ply][1].to) {
            m.score = 80000;
            continue;
        }
        // History
        m.score = gHistory[m.from][m.to];
    }
    
    sort(moves.begin(), moves.end(), [](const Move& a, const Move& b) {
        return a.score > b.score;
    });
    
    int bestScore = -INF_SCORE;
    Move bestMove = {0, 0, 0, 0, 0};
    int legalMoves = 0;
    int ttFlag = TT_UPPER;
    
    for (int i = 0; i < (int)moves.size(); i++) {
        Move& m = moves[i];
        
        UndoInfo undo = makeMove(b, m);
        
        // Check legality
        if (isAttacked(b, b.kingSq[b.side ^ 1], b.side)) {
            unmakeMove(b, m, undo);
            continue;
        }
        
        legalMoves++;
        int score;
        
        // Late move reductions
        bool isCapture = (undo.captured != EMPTY);
        if (legalMoves >= 4 && depth >= 3 && !isCapture && !inCheck && m.promotion == 0) {
            int reduction = 1 + (legalMoves >= 8);
            score = -alphaBeta(b, depth - 1 - reduction, -alpha - 1, -alpha, ply + 1);
            if (score > alpha && !gSearchStopped) {
                score = -alphaBeta(b, depth - 1, -beta, -alpha, ply + 1);
            }
        } else {
            // PVS: search first move with full window, then with null window
            if (legalMoves == 1) {
                score = -alphaBeta(b, depth - 1, -beta, -alpha, ply + 1);
            } else {
                score = -alphaBeta(b, depth - 1, -alpha - 1, -alpha, ply + 1);
                if (score > alpha && score < beta && !gSearchStopped) {
                    score = -alphaBeta(b, depth - 1, -beta, -alpha, ply + 1);
                }
            }
        }
        
        unmakeMove(b, m, undo);
        
        if (gSearchStopped) return 0;
        
        if (score > bestScore) {
            bestScore = score;
            bestMove = m;
            if (ply == 0) {
                gBestMove = m;
                gBestScore = score;
            }
        }
        
        if (score > alpha) {
            alpha = score;
            ttFlag = TT_EXACT;
        }
        
        if (alpha >= beta) {
            ttFlag = TT_LOWER;
            // Update killer moves (only for quiet moves)
            if (!isCapture) {
                gKillers[ply][1] = gKillers[ply][0];
                gKillers[ply][0] = m;
                gHistory[m.from][m.to] += depth * depth;
            }
            break;
        }
    }
    
    // No legal moves: checkmate or stalemate
    if (legalMoves == 0) {
        if (inCheck) return -MATE_SCORE + ply; // checkmate
        else return 0; // stalemate
    }
    
    // Store in TT
    gTT[ttIndex] = {key, (int16_t)bestScore, (int8_t)depth, (uint8_t)ttFlag, (uint8_t)bestMove.from, (uint8_t)bestMove.to};
    
    return bestScore;
}
```

Wait, I'm using PVS (Principal Variation Search) combined with LMR. The PVS part is:
1. Search the first move with full window (-beta, -alpha)
2. For subsequent moves, search with null window (-alpha-1, -alpha)
3. If the null window search returns a score > alpha, re-search with full window

The LMR part is:
1. For moves late in the move list (after the first few), search with reduced depth
2. If the reduced search returns a score > alpha, re-search with full depth

These can be combined:
- For the first move: search with full window and full depth
- For subsequent moves:
  - If eligible for LMR: search with reduced depth and null window. If score > alpha, re-search with full depth and null window. If still > alpha, re-search with full depth and full window.
  - If not eligible for LMR: search with null window and full depth. If score > alpha, re-search with full window and full depth.

This is the standard approach. Let me implement it.

Actually, let me simplify. The LMR + PVS combination can be:

```cpp
int score;
if (legalMoves == 1) {
    // First move: full window, full depth
    score = -alphaBeta(b, depth - 1, -beta, -alpha, ply + 1);
} else {
    // LMR
    int reduction = 0;
    if (legalMoves >= 4 && depth >= 3 && !isCapture && !inCheck && !m.promotion) {
        reduction = 1 + (legalMoves >= 8);
    }
    
    // Null window search with possible reduction
    score = -alphaBeta(b, depth - 1 - reduction, -alpha - 1, -alpha, ply + 1);
    
    // Re-search with full depth if LMR was applied and score > alpha
    if (reduction > 0 && score > alpha && !gSearchStopped) {
        score = -alphaBeta(b, depth - 1, -alpha - 1, -alpha, ply + 1);
    }
    
    // Re-search with full window if score > alpha (PVS)
    if (score > alpha && score < beta && !gSearchStopped) {
        score = -alphaBeta(b, depth - 1, -beta, -alpha, ply + 1);
    }
}
```

This is the standard approach. Let me use it.

OK, I think I have all the pieces. Let me write the complete code now.

Let me also handle one more thing: mate score adjustment in the TT. When storing a mate score, I need to adjust it to be relative to the root. When retrieving, I need to adjust it back.

When I detect checkmate at ply P, the score is -MATE_SCORE + P. When storing this in the TT, I should store it relative to the root, i.e., -MATE_SCORE + P - rootPly. But since I don't have rootPly in the TT, I'll store it as -MATE_SCORE + P and adjust when retrieving.

Actually, the standard approach is:
- When storing: if score is a mate score, adjust it to be relative to the position (not the root): mateScore = score + ply (for positive mate scores) or mateScore = score - ply (for negative mate scores)
  
Wait, I need to think about this more carefully. The score at ply P is -MATE_SCORE + P (for a checkmate at ply P). This means checkmate in P - rootPly moves from the root.

When storing in the TT, I want to store a score that's independent of the search path. So I should store: adjustedScore = score + ply if score > MATE_SCORE - 100, or adjustedScore = score - ply if score < -MATE_SCORE + 100.

When retrieving from the TT, I should reverse the adjustment: score = adjustedScore - ply if adjustedScore > MATE_SCORE - 100, or score = adjustedScore + ply if adjustedScore < -MATE_SCORE + 100.

Wait, let me think about this again. The issue is that the same position can be reached at different plies in the search tree. The TT should store the score relative to the position, not the ply.

Score at ply P: checkmate in N plies = MATE_SCORE - N.
But N is the number of plies from the current position to checkmate. So N = (MATE_SCORE - score) where score = -MATE_SCORE + P + (MATE_SCORE - N) ... hmm, this is getting confusing.

- At ply 2, we find that the position is checkmate in 1 ply. Score = MATE_SCORE - 1.

But wait, in negamax, the score is relative to the side to move. A checkmate for the side to move is a very negative score (they're being checkmated). A checkmate for the opponent is a very positive score.

- At ply P, if the side to move has no legal moves and is in check, it's checkmate. The score is -MATE_SCORE + P (distance from root). But actually, the score should represent the distance from the current position, not from the root.

Hmm, the standard convention in chess engines is:
- Checkmate score = MATE_SCORE - distance_from_root
- This means a checkmate found sooner (at a lower ply) has a higher score, which is what we want.

When storing in the TT:
- If score > MATE_SCORE - MAX_DEPTH, it's a positive mate score. Store as score + ply (to make it distance-independent).
- If score < -MATE_SCORE + MAX_DEPTH, it's a negative mate score. Store as score - ply (to make it distance-independent).

When retrieving from the TT:
- If storedScore > MATE_SCORE - MAX_DEPTH, it's a positive mate score. Return storedScore - ply.
- If storedScore < -MATE_SCORE + MAX_DEPTH, it's a negative mate score. Return storedScore + ply.

Wait, let me think about this more carefully.

If at ply 3, the score is MATE_SCORE - 3 (checkmate in 3 plies from root, or equivalently, 0 plies from the current position since the opponent is checkmated right now).

When I store this in the TT, I want to store it such that when retrieved at a different ply, the score is correct. If the same position is reached at ply 5, the score should be MATE_SCORE - 5 (because it's 5 plies from the root, but the same position).

When retrieved at ply 5: score = storedScore - 5 = MATE_SCORE - 5. Correct!

For negative mate scores:
At ply 3, the score is -MATE_SCORE + 3 (we're being checkmated).
storedScore = -MATE_SCORE + 3 - 3 = -MATE_SCORE (I subtract the ply).
When retrieved at ply 5: score = storedScore + 5 = -MATE_SCORE + 5. Correct!

So the adjustment is:
- Store: if score > MATE_SCORE - MAX_DEPTH, store score + ply; if score < -MATE_SCORE + MAX_DEPTH, store score - ply.
- Retrieve: if storedScore > MATE_SCORE - MAX_DEPTH, return storedScore - ply; if storedScore < -MATE_SCORE + MAX_DEPTH, return storedScore + ply.

Wait, but the stored score MATE_SCORE is always > MATE_SCORE - MAX_DEPTH (assuming MAX_DEPTH > 0). So the condition is always true for mate scores. I need a threshold that distinguishes mate scores from normal scores.

The threshold is typically MATE_SCORE - MAX_DEPTH. If the score is greater than this, it's a positive mate score. If it's less than -MATE_SCORE + MAX_DEPTH, it's a negative mate score.

Let me use MATE_SCORE = 49000 and MAX_DEPTH = 128. So the threshold is 49000 - 128 = 48872. Any score > 48872 is a positive mate score. Any score < -48872 is a negative mate score.

Let me think about the output format one more time. The move notation:
- Piece letter: 'p' for pawn, 'N' for knight, 'B' for bishop, 'R' for rook, 'Q' for queen, 'K' for king
- Source square
- 'x' if capture
- Destination square
- '/Q' etc. for promotion
- 'ep' for en passant
- '+' for check, '#' for checkmate

Wait, the problem says:
- Piece letter (lowercase p for pawn, uppercase N/B/R/Q/K for others) + source square + destination square.
- Use "x" between source and destination for captures: `pe4xd5`
- Promotion: append `/` and the piece letter, e.g. `pe7e8/Q`
- Castling: `O-O` (kingside) or `O-O-O` (queenside).
- En passant: append `ep`, e.g. `pe5xd6ep`
- Check: append `+`, e.g. `Bb4c5+`
- Checkmate: append `#`, e.g. `Qd1h5#`

So the format is:
- [piece_letter][source_square]["x"][dest_square]["/"promotion_piece]["ep"]["+" or "#"]
- For castling: "O-O" or "O-O-O" (with possible "+" or "#")

For captures, the "x" goes between source and destination. So: pe4xd5 (pawn from e4 captures on d5).

For non-captures: pe2e4 (pawn from e2 to e4).

For promotion: pe7e8/Q (pawn from e7 to e8, promotes to queen). If it's a capture promotion: pe7xd8/Q.

For en passant: pe5xd6ep (pawn from e5 captures en passant to d6). Note the "x" is included because it's a capture.

For check: Bb4c5+ (bishop from b4 to c5, gives check).

For checkmate: Qd1h5# (queen from d1 to h5, checkmate).

Let me make sure I handle all these cases correctly in the move notation function.

```cpp
string moveToNotation(const Board& b, const Move& m) {
    if (m.flags == FLAG_CASTLE) {
        string s;
        if (fileOf(m.to) == 6) s = "O-O";
        else s = "O-O-O";
        // Check for check/checkmate
        Board copy = b;
        UndoInfo undo = makeMove(copy, m);
        // Note: after makeMove, copy.side has flipped
        bool inCheck = isAttacked(copy, copy.kingSq[copy.side], copy.side ^ 1);
        if (inCheck) {
            // Check if it's checkmate
            vector<Move> legalMoves = generateLegalMoves(copy);
            if (legalMoves.empty()) s += "#";
            else s += "+";
        }
        unmakeMove(copy, m, undo);
        return s;
    }
    
    string s;
    int pt = pieceType(b.board[m.from]);
    
    // Piece letter
    if (pt == PAWN) s += 'p';
    else s += " NBRQK"[pt]; // KNIGHT=2 -> 'N', BISHOP=3 -> 'B', etc.
    
    // Source square
    s += sqToStr(m.from);
    
    // Capture
    bool isCapture = (b.board[m.to] != EMPTY) || (m.flags == FLAG_EP);
    if (isCapture) s += 'x';
    
    // Destination square
    s += sqToStr(m.to);
    
    // Promotion
    if (m.promotion) {
        s += '/';
        switch (m.promotion) {
            case QUEEN: s += 'Q'; break;
            case ROOK: s += 'R'; break;
            case BISHOP: s += 'B'; break;
            case KNIGHT: s += 'N'; break;
        }
    }
    
    // En passant
    if (m.flags == FLAG_EP) s += "ep";
    
    // Check/checkmate
    Board copy = b;
    UndoInfo undo = makeMove(copy, m);
    bool inCheck = isAttacked(copy, copy.kingSq[copy.side], copy.side ^ 1);
    if (inCheck) {
        vector<Move> legalMoves = generateLegalMoves(copy);
        if (legalMoves.empty()) s += '#';
        else s += '+';
    }
    unmakeMove(copy, m, undo);
    
    return s;
}
```

Wait, for the piece letter, I'm using " NBRQK" indexed by pt. Let me check:
- pt = KNIGHT = 2: " NBRQK"[2] = 'N'. Wait, let me count: " NBRQK"[0] = ' ', [1] = 'N', [2] = 'B'. That's wrong.

```cpp
vector<Move> generateLegalMoves(Board& b) {
    vector<Move> legal;
    vector<Move> pseudo = generatePseudoLegal(b);
    for (const auto& m : pseudo) {
        UndoInfo undo = makeMove(b, m);
        if (!isAttacked(b, b.kingSq[b.side ^ 1], b.side)) {
            legal.push_back(m);
        }
        unmakeMove(b, m, undo);
    }
    return legal;
}
```

Let me also add the aspiration window to the iterative deepening loop:

```cpp
for (int depth = 1; depth <= MAX_DEPTH; depth++) {
    int alpha = -INF_SCORE;
    int beta = INF_SCORE;
    
    if (depth >= 4 && abs(gBestScore) < MATE_SCORE - MAX_DEPTH) {
        alpha = gBestScore - 50;
        beta = gBestScore + 50;
    }
    
    int score = alphaBeta(gBoard, depth, alpha, beta, 0);
    
    // If search failed outside aspiration window, re-search with full window
    if ((score <= alpha || score >= beta) && !gSearchStopped) {
        score = alphaBeta(gBoard, depth, -INF_SCORE, INF_SCORE, 0);
    }
    
    if (gSearchStopped) break;
    
    gBestScore = score;
    
    // Check time
    auto elapsed = duration_cast<milliseconds>(steady_clock::now() - gStartTime).count();
    if (elapsed > gTimeLimit / 2) break;
}
```

Hmm, actually aspiration windows can be tricky. If the search fails low (score <= alpha), I should re-search with (alpha = -INF, beta = alpha + 1) or something like that. Let me simplify and not use aspiration windows for now.

Actually, let me use a simple aspiration window with widening:

```cpp
int aspAlpha = -INF_SCORE;
int aspBeta = INF_SCORE;

for (int depth = 1; depth <= MAX_DEPTH; depth++) {
    if (depth >= 4 && abs(gBestScore) < MATE_SCORE - MAX_DEPTH) {
        aspAlpha = gBestScore - 50;
        aspBeta = gBestScore + 50;
    }
    
    int score;
    while (true) {
        score = alphaBeta(gBoard, depth, aspAlpha, aspBeta, 0);
        if (gSearchStopped) break;
        
        if (score <= aspAlpha) {
            aspAlpha = -INF_SCORE; // widen lower bound
        } else if (score >= aspBeta) {
            aspBeta = INF_SCORE; // widen upper bound
        } else {
            break; // score is within the window
        }
    }
    
    if (gSearchStopped) break;
    
    gBestScore = score;
    
    auto elapsed = duration_cast<milliseconds>(steady_clock::now() - gStartTime).count();
    if (elapsed > gTimeLimit / 2) break;
}
```

This is a simple aspiration window with widening. If the score falls outside the window, I widen the window and re-search.

```cpp
#include <iostream>
#include <string>
#include <vector>
#include <algorithm>
#include <chrono>
#include <cstring>
#include <thread>
#include <atomic>
#include <mutex>

using namespace std;
using namespace chrono;

// Piece types
enum PieceType { EMPTY_PIECE = 0, PAWN = 1, KNIGHT = 2, BISHOP = 3, ROOK = 4, QUEEN = 5, KING = 6 };
enum Color { WHITE = 0, BLACK = 1 };

// Piece encoding: color * 6 + type (1-6)
// 0 = empty, 1-6 = white pieces, 7-12 = black pieces
inline int makePiece(int color, int type) { return color * 6 + type; }
inline int pieceType(int piece) { return piece == 0 ? 0 : ((piece - 1) % 6) + 1; }
inline int pieceColor(int piece) { return piece == 0 ? 0 : (piece - 1) / 6; }

// Square encoding: rank * 8 + file
// rank 0 = 1st rank, file 0 = a-file
inline int makeSquare(int rank, int file) { return rank * 8 + file; }
inline int rankOf(int sq) { return sq >> 3; }
inline int fileOf(int sq) { return sq & 7; }
inline string squareStr(int sq) {
    return string(1, 'a' + fileOf(sq)) + string(1, '1' + rankOf(sq));
}

// Piece to character for move notation
char pieceChar(int pt) {
    switch (pt) {
        case PAWN: return 'p';
        case KNIGHT: return 'N';
        case BISHOP: return 'B';
        case ROOK: return 'R';
        case QUEEN: return 'Q';
        case KING: return 'K';
        default: return '?';
    }
}

// Move representation
struct Move {
    int from, to;
    int captured; // piece captured (0 if none)
    int promotion; // piece type to promote to (0 if none)
    int flags; // bit 0: en passant, bit 1: castling, bit 2: double push
    
    bool isEnPassant() const { return flags & 1; }
    bool isCastling() const { return flags & 2; }
    bool isDoublePush() const { return flags & 4; }
    bool isCapture() const { return captured != 0 || isEnPassant(); }
    bool isPromotion() const { return promotion != 0; }
};

// ... and so on
```

Let me think about the move notation more carefully:

- Normal move: `pieceChar + sourceSquare + destSquare` (e.g., `pe2e4`, `Ng1f3`)
- Capture: `pieceChar + sourceSquare + "x" + destSquare` (e.g., `pe4xd5`, `Nf3xe5`)
- Promotion: append `"/" + promotionChar` (e.g., `pe7e8/Q`, `pe7xd8/Q`)
- Castling: `O-O` or `O-O-O`
- En passant: append `ep` (e.g., `pe5xd6ep`)
- Check: append `+`
- Checkmate: append `#`

The check/checkmate is determined after making the move. So I need to:
1. Generate the move

Actually, I realize there's a subtlety with the en passant square in FEN. The FEN records the en passant target square, which is the square the pawn would move to when capturing en passant. Let me think about the move generation more carefully:

**Pawn moves:**
- Single push: pawn moves one rank forward (if square is empty)
- Double push: pawn moves two ranks forward from starting position (if both squares are empty)
- Captures: pawn captures diagonally forward (if enemy piece is there)
- En passant: pawn captures en passant (if ep square is available and pawn is adjacent)
- Promotion: if pawn reaches last rank, promote to N/B/R/Q

For white, pawns move in the +rank direction. For black, pawns move in the -rank direction.

Starting rank for white pawns: 1 (2nd rank)
Starting rank for black pawns: 6 (7th rank)
Promotion rank for white: 7 (8th rank)
Promotion rank for black: 0 (1st rank)

**Knight moves:**
The 8 possible offsets from a square: (-2,-1), (-2,1), (-1,-2), (-1,2), (1,-2), (1,2), (2,-1), (2,1)

**Bishop moves:**
Diagonal directions: (1,1), (1,-1), (-1,1), (-1,-1)

**Rook moves:**
Straight directions: (1,0), (-1,0), (0,1), (0,-1)

**Queen moves:**
All 8 directions.

**King moves:**
All 8 directions, one step. Plus castling.

**Castling:**
White kingside: King from e1 to g1, rook from h1 to f1
White queenside: King from e1 to c1, rook from a1 to d1
Black kingside: King from e8 to g8, rook from h8 to f8
Black queenside: King from e8 to c8, rook from a8 to d8

Castling requirements:
- The king and rook haven't moved (castling rights)
- No pieces between king and rook
- King is not in check
- King doesn't pass through check
- King doesn't end up in check

For the castling rights, I'll use 4 bits:
- Bit 0: White kingside (K)
- Bit 1: White queenside (Q)
- Bit 2: Black kingside (k)
- Bit 3: Black queenside (q)

When the king moves, both castling rights for that side are lost.
When a rook moves from its starting square, the corresponding castling right is lost.
When a rook is captured on its starting square, the corresponding castling right is lost.

OK, let me write the code now. I'll use a class-based approach.

Actually, for make/unmake, I need to be careful. Let me think about what I need to undo:

Let me think about how to handle the en passant capture. When a pawn captures en passant, the captured pawn is on a different square than the destination square. I need to know where the captured pawn is to undo the move.

In the standard en passant case:
- White pawn on e5 captures en passant on d6: the captured pawn is on d5
- The destination square (d6) is the en passant target square

So when making an en passant capture, I remove the pawn from the square (to.rank - 1, to.file) for white, or (to.rank + 1, to.file) for black.

Wait, let me think again. If white plays e5xd6 ep, the white pawn moves from e5 to d6, and the black pawn on d5 is captured. So the captured pawn is on (to.rank - 1, to.file) = (5-1, 3) = (4, 3) = d5. Yes, that's correct.

For black playing d4xe3 ep, the black pawn moves from d4 to e3, and the white pawn on e4 is captured. The captured pawn is on (to.rank + 1, to.file) = (2+1, 4) = (3, 4) = e4. Yes, that's correct.

So the captured pawn in en passant is at makeSquare(rankOf(to) + (side == WHITE ? -1 : 1), fileOf(to)).

Wait no. If white captures ep, the white pawn moves to the ep target square (which is on rank 5, e.g., d6). The captured black pawn is one rank below, on rank 4 (e.g., d5). So captured pawn rank = rankOf(to) - 1 when side == WHITE.

If black captures ep, the black pawn moves to the ep target square (which is on rank 2, e.g., e3). The captured white pawn is one rank above, on rank 3 (e.g., e4). So captured pawn rank = rankOf(to) + 1 when side == BLACK.

In general: captured pawn rank = rankOf(to) - pawnDir, where pawnDir is +1 for white and -1 for black.

Wait, white pawns move in the +rank direction, so pawnDir for white is +1. The ep target square for white is on rank 5 (0-indexed), and the captured pawn is on rank 4. So captured pawn rank = rankOf(to) - 1 = rankOf(to) - pawnDir.

Similarly, black pawns move in the -rank direction, so pawnDir for black is -1. The ep target square for black is on rank 2 (0-indexed), and the captured pawn is on rank 3. So captured pawn rank = rankOf(to) + 1 = rankOf(to) - pawnDir (since pawnDir = -1, -pawnDir = +1).

Wait, that doesn't work. Let me re-derive.

For white: pawnDir = +1 (pawns move towards higher ranks)
  ep target is on rank 5, captured pawn is on rank 4
  captured pawn rank = ep target rank - 1 = rankOf(to) - 1

For black: pawnDir = -1 (pawns move towards lower ranks)
  ep target is on rank 2, captured pawn is on rank 3
  captured pawn rank = ep target rank + 1 = rankOf(to) + 1

So captured pawn rank = rankOf(to) - pawnDir... wait.

For white: pawnDir = +1, rankOf(to) - pawnDir = rankOf(to) - 1. Correct.
For black: pawnDir = -1, rankOf(to) - pawnDir = rankOf(to) + 1. Correct.

So capturedPawnSq = makeSquare(rankOf(to) - pawnDir, fileOf(to)).

Wait, but pawnDir should be the direction the capturing pawn moves. For white, it's +1 (towards higher ranks). For the ep capture, white moves up, so the captured pawn is behind (below) the destination. So captured pawn rank = dest rank - 1.

For black, pawnDir is -1 (towards lower ranks). The captured pawn is behind (above) the destination. So captured pawn rank = dest rank + 1.

capturedPawnRank = rankOf(to) - pawnDir[side]
where pawnDir[WHITE] = +1, pawnDir[BLACK] = -1.

rankOf(to) - pawnDir[WHITE] = rankOf(to) - 1 ✓
rankOf(to) - pawnDir[BLACK] = rankOf(to) - (-1) = rankOf(to) + 1 ✓

Great!

One more thing: I need to be careful about the FEN parsing. The FEN has 6 fields:
1. Piece placement
2. Active color

4. En passant target square
5. Halfmove clock
6. Fullmove number

For the piece placement, I parse each rank from left to right, starting from rank 8 (top) to rank 1 (bottom). Numbers represent empty squares.

Let me write the code:

```cpp
void parseFEN(const string& fen) {
    memset(board, 0, sizeof(board));
    int rank = 7, file = 0;
    int i = 0;
    
    // Piece placement
    while (i < fen.size() && fen[i] != ' ') {
        if (fen[i] == '/') {
            rank--;
            file = 0;
        } else if (fen[i] >= '1' && fen[i] <= '8') {
            file += fen[i] - '0';
        } else {
            int piece = charToPiece(fen[i]);
            int sq = makeSquare(rank, file);
            board[sq] = piece;
            if (pieceType(piece) == KING) kingSquare[pieceColor(piece)] = sq;
            file++;
        }
        i++;
    }
    i++; // skip space
    
    // Active color
    side = (fen[i] == 'w') ? WHITE : BLACK;
    i += 2; // skip color and space
    
    // Castling availability
    castling = 0;
    while (i < fen.size() && fen[i] != ' ') {
        switch (fen[i]) {
            case 'K': castling |= 1; break;
            case 'Q': castling |= 2; break;
            case 'k': castling |= 4; break;
            case 'q': castling |= 8; break;
        }
        i++;
    }
    i++; // skip space
    
    // En passant target square
    if (fen[i] == '-') {
        epSquare = -1;
        i++;
    } else {
        int epFile = fen[i] - 'a';
        int epRank = fen[i+1] - '1';
        epSquare = makeSquare(epRank, epFile);
        i += 2;
    }
    i++; // skip space
    
    // Halfmove clock
    halfmove = 0;
    while (i < fen.size() && fen[i] != ' ') {
        halfmove = halfmove * 10 + (fen[i] - '0');
        i++;
    }
    i++; // skip space
    
    // Fullmove number
    fullmove = 0;
    while (i < fen.size()) {
        fullmove = fullmove * 10 + (fen[i] - '0');
        i++;
    }
    
    // Compute Zobrist hash
    computeHash();
}
```

OK, let me now write the complete code. This will be very long but I need to get it right.

Let me also think about the move ordering. Good move ordering is critical for alpha-beta pruning. I'll use:
1. Transposition table move (best move from previous search)
2. Captures, ordered by MVV-LVA (Most Valuable Victim - Least Valuable Attacker)
3. Killer moves (quiet moves that caused beta cutoff at the same depth)
4. History heuristic (quiet moves ordered by how often they caused cutoffs)

For the quiescence search, I'll search all captures until a quiet position is reached. I'll also use delta pruning to skip obviously bad captures.

Let me also think about null move pruning. In non-pawn endgames and when not in check, I can try a "null move" (passing the turn) and search with a reduced depth. If the null move fails high, I can prune the branch.

And late move reductions (LMR): for moves late in the move list (which are likely to be bad), I can search with a reduced depth first, and only re-search at full depth if the reduced search fails high.

OK, let me write the complete code now. I'll aim for a strong but correct implementation.

- Zobrist hash (for collision detection)

- Type (exact, lower bound, upper bound)

I'll use a replacement policy based on depth (prefer deeper entries).

```cpp
struct TTEntry {
    uint64_t hash;    // 8 bytes
    int16_t score;    // 2 bytes
    int16_t depth;    // 2 bytes
    uint8_t type;     // 1 byte (EXACT, LOWER, UPPER)
    uint8_t padding;  // 1 byte
    Move bestMove;    // needs to be compact
};
```

Wait, Move is currently a struct with several fields. For the TT, I need a compact representation. Let me use a 16-bit encoding: 6 bits for from, 6 bits for to, 3 bits for promotion, 1 bit for flags. That's 16 bits total.

Actually, let me use a 32-bit encoding for compact moves:
- bits 0-5: from square (6 bits)
- bits 6-11: to square (6 bits)
- bits 12-14: promotion piece type (3 bits, 0 if no promotion)
- bit 15: en passant flag
- bit 16: castling flag
- bits 17-31: unused

That fits in 32 bits.

```cpp
typedef uint32_t CompactMove;

CompactMove packMove(const Move& m) {
    return m.from | (m.to << 6) | (m.promotion << 12) | 
           ((m.isEnPassant() ? 1 : 0) << 15) | ((m.isCastling() ? 1 : 0) << 16);
}

Move unpackMove(CompactMove cm) {
    Move m;
    m.from = cm & 63;
    m.to = (cm >> 6) & 63;
    m.promotion = (cm >> 12) & 7;
    m.flags = ((cm >> 15) & 1) | (((cm >> 16) & 1) << 1);
    m.captured = 0; // will be filled in later
    return m;
}
```

Then the TT entry can be:
```cpp
struct TTEntry {
    uint64_t hash;      // 8 bytes
    int16_t score;      // 2 bytes
    uint8_t depth;      // 1 byte (depth up to 255)
    uint8_t type;       // 1 byte
    CompactMove best;   // 4 bytes
};
// Total: 16 bytes
```

With 16 bytes per entry and 256 MB, that's 16 million entries. That should be plenty.

Actually, let me just use a power of 2 for the table size. 2^24 = 16 million entries × 16 bytes = 256 MB.

